    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer6870579873398121045">Seventeen-year-old Caymen Meyers studies the rich like her own personal science experiment, and after years of observation she’s pretty sure they’re only good for one thing—spending money on useless stuff, like the porcelain dolls in her mother’s shop.<br/><br/>So when Xander Spence walks into the store to pick up a doll for his grandmother, it only takes one glance for Caymen to fi</span>
  <span id="freeText6870579873398121045" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Caymen Meyers studies the rich like her own personal science experiment, and after years of observation she’s pretty sure they’re only good for one thing—spending money on useless stuff, like the porcelain dolls in her mother’s shop.<br /><br />So when Xander Spence walks into the store to pick up a doll for his grandmother, it only takes one glance for Caymen to figure out he’s oozing rich. Despite his charming ways and that he’s one of the first people who actually gets her, she’s smart enough to know his interest won’t last. Because if there’s one thing she’s learned from her mother’s warnings, it’s that the rich have a short attention span. But Xander keeps coming around, despite her best efforts to scare him off. And much to her dismay, she's beginning to enjoy his company.<br /><br />She knows her mom can’t find out—she wouldn’t approve. She’d much rather Caymen hang out with the local rocker who hasn’t been raised by money. But just when Xander’s attention and loyalty are about to convince Caymen that being rich isn’t a character flaw, she finds out that money is a much bigger part of their relationship than she’d ever realized. And that Xander’s not the only one she should’ve been worried about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6870579873398121045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">@Quaylynn Madden<br/>I honestly don't think there needs to be sequel to understand this book.<br/>What happens to the doll store?---<br/>Susan now has her parents ba<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">@Quaylynn Madden<br />I honestly don't think there needs to be sequel to understand this book.<br />What happens to the doll store?---<br />Susan now has her parents back,so she doesn't need to live by her own.She'll now live with her parents.<br />Does Caymen's mother and Xander form a relationship?--<br />Yeah. Cause in the hospital Susan said to Caymen that she has an apology to make to Xander.<br />Does Caymen and her grandparents form a relationship?--<br />Yes,I'm sure they will.Because when Susan was in the hospital they were living with Caymen,which means Caymen has forgiven them and her grandparents told how sweet she was so I don't think there's a chance that they wont.<br />What does Caymen decide to do for her life?--<br />She'll go to UNLV, or maybe some other college (but probably UNLV) and do major in science (CRIME INVESTIGATION).And live with her grandparents and be the girlfriend of Xander Spence.<br />Does Xander take after his father?--<br />Yeah,Cause Xander's really good in many fields so he'll take over his family business (i.e.The Road's End Hotel).<br />Does Caymen meet her dad?--<br />No,she won't.Because now that she has her mom,her grandparents and Xander ,she wouldn't do it.<br />Will Susan live?--<br />Yeah,she will.The Doctor said it was a treatable condition,so yeah,she will live.<br />I hope this answered all your questions.! :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1690524870" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1690524870" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1690524870?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=rich-vs-poor">rich-vs-poor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1690524870" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10421918805549383229"><strong>3.5 stars</strong><br/><br/>I definitely need a bit of self-berating right now.<br/><br/>I put off reading this book for so long and that because I was certain it would fall into my heap of a pile of ever-growing clichéd love stories read.<br/><br/>But it didn’t! Well… it didn’t fall <em>that </em>far from said pile, but what counts is where it landed in the end and that is in my ‘‘guilty pleasure’’ pile.<br/><br/>That’s right, Kasie West is one hell of a guilty pleasure writer for me.<br/><br/>Truth be told, the skeleton of her novels is always a little overuse</span>
  <span id="freeText10421918805549383229" style="display:none"><strong>3.5 stars</strong><br /><br />I definitely need a bit of self-berating right now.<br /><br />I put off reading this book for so long and that because I was certain it would fall into my heap of a pile of ever-growing clichéd love stories read.<br /><br />But it didn’t! Well… it didn’t fall <em>that </em>far from said pile, but what counts is where it landed in the end and that is in my ‘‘guilty pleasure’’ pile.<br /><br />That’s right, Kasie West is one hell of a guilty pleasure writer for me.<br /><br />Truth be told, the skeleton of her novels is always a little overused. For instance, <em>The Distance Between Us</em> relates the story of a poor teenage girl who falls in love with a rich teenage boy.<br /><br />BUT. What is special about this author is that the <em>meat </em>on the skeleton is fresh.<br /><br />(Well that metaphor sure was morbid.)<br /><br />Take Caymen. She has one hell of a dry humor, and unlike most teen girls her age, she’s not in search of a boyfriend. And neither is Xander. Of a girlfriend.<br /><br />They have a charming story of the first time they met—at a doll shop.<br /><br />And the way they spend time in each other's company is also very original. See, they both have a hazy idea of what their ideal future would be—what they’d like to do, who they’d like to be—so they schedule these weekly-based meetings to plenty of fun (*inserts cackle*) places that could sparkle something inside of them, like an epiphany regarding their future.<br /><br />It’s very, very fun.<br /><br />Sure, the skeleton remains, so yes there will be clichéd situations—but that’s okay. It will not obstruct you from enjoying the story.<br /><br />Those were some really great four hours I spent reading <em>The Distance Between Us. </em>An afternoon well spent.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10421918805549383229" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_419211302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419211302" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419211302?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who love sarcasm and cute romances</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=just-take-my-heart-already">just-take-my-heart-already</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=really-looking-forward-to-this-book">really-looking-forward-to-this-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=gave-away">gave-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-favorite">2013-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-relationships">best-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419211302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2200883896658999218"><br/>Actual rating: 4.5<br/><br/>That's it. Kasie West is now one of my new favorite authors. After being completely <a title='Review: Pivot Point by Kasie West' href='http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/02/26/review-pivot-point-by-kasie-west/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>swept off my feet</a> by <em>Pivot Point</em>, West has once again warmed my heart with so many cute moments. She continuously manages to create down to earth, relatable characters and all-around fun books.<br/><br/><em>The Distance Between Us</em> follows Caymen Meyers, a girl who has certain opinions about rich people thanks to her mother's clear disdain. Her mom has raised her to think very negatively about the Haves verses</span>
  <span id="freeText2200883896658999218" style="display:none"><br>Actual rating: 4.5<br><br>That's it. Kasie West is now one of my new favorite authors. After being completely <a title="Review: Pivot Point by Kasie West" href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2013/02/26/review-pivot-point-by-kasie-west/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">swept off my feet</a> by <em>Pivot Point</em>, West has once again warmed my heart with so many cute moments. She continuously manages to create down to earth, relatable characters and all-around fun books.<br><br><em>The Distance Between Us</em> follows Caymen Meyers, a girl who has certain opinions about rich people thanks to her mother's clear disdain. Her mom has raised her to think very negatively about the Haves verses the Have Nots due to her own troubled past with a rich ex-boyfriend. So naturally, when rich boy Xander Spence walks into their doll shop and "beckons" her, she's pretty much already had her mind made up. But in a strange turn of events they begin spending more time together on these "career days." What happens next can only be described as one of the most ADORBS books you can ever read!<br><br>While the novel is more romance centered, West never spares her characters room to grow and develop. The time Caymen spends with Xander shows her that her mother's bias is just that, bias based on her own experiences. In fact, Xander himself is the one to acknowledge that both he and Caymen aren't that different regardless of income level. Thus, these "career days" are born which helps reveal what they each want to do with their lives despite parental expectations placed on them. And through this, an unlikely friendship blossoms and later turns to first love.<br><br>I absolutely loved this story to bits. There was't a moment I was bored or not entertained thanks to the AWESOME sarcasm from Caymen. It's not the kind everyone will enjoy, but it was just right for me, leaving me laughing out loud at almost every page. And when I wasn't laughing, I was sighing at the perfect dialogue between Xander an Caymen.<br><blockquote>“Caymen?”<br>“Yes?”<br>“You look terrified. Does this scare you?”<br>“More than anything.”<br>“Why?”<br>“Because I didn’t bring my mints.”<br>“And now the real answer . . .”<br>“Because I’m afraid that once you catch me, the game’s over.”</blockquote><br>*Happy sigh*<br><br>Kasie West writes the type of romance I love to read. It's not cheesy or over the top. It's not unbelievable  or unrealistic. It doesn't make you roll your eyes or make your head collide with a wall from frustration. It's the kind that makes you all giddy inside. The kind that gets your feels all "a meltin'" and the type that makes you twirl around in your living room like your a Disney Princess.<br><br><img alt=" photo twirl_zpsbbf7953a.gif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391957ra/754685.gif" width="500" height="219" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>And that's the best kind of feeling ever!</em><br><br>Final verdict: I'd highly recommend this totally adorable book. If you're in a reading slump and you need a book to bring a smile to your face, this is your book. If you are looking to be entertained, look no further. If you are just looking for a cute read that will wrap your heart up in a blanket made of feels, read this book and twirl, my friends. Weeeeeee!<br><br><br><em>ARC was received from Amy of <a href="http://www.booklovingme.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Loving Mom</a>. Thanks again, Amy!</em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2200883896658999218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1253365751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253365751" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253365751?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shelby *trains flying monkeys* by: </span>

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430861279ra/14771825.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Umm..it's more like this:<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/4rSSW7k' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430861279i/14771826._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>She works all the hours she can spare for her mom and plans on putting off college for awhile because she wants to make sure her mom will be okay. <br/>She doesn't party. She </span>
  <span id="freeText9444003849822813952" style="display:none">If you go into a normal young adult romance book you expect this:<br><a href="http://imgur.com/2BScTW9" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430861279ra/14771823.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book is not that. It's more of this:<br><a href="http://imgur.com/4qESMgt" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430861279ra/14771824.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430861279i/14771826._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She works all the hours she can spare for her mom and plans on putting off college for awhile because she wants to make sure her mom will be okay. <br>She doesn't party. She does not fall into insta-love.<br>She does not like to be pressured into things.<br> <b>I put up my hands. "Oh, I don't drink. I'm seventeen."<br>"So? I'm nineteen."<br>"My mom says before I turn eighteen she still has the right to murder me." My mom always tells me to blame it on her if I am ever in an uncomfortable situation. It seems to work well.</b><br><br>She does not tone herself down to impress the "boy"...<br> <b>"Note to self: Caymen is very good at sarcasm."<br>"If you're recording notes for an official record. I'd like the word 'very' stricken and replaced with 'exceptionally.'"</b><br><br>The boy she meets at her mom's doll shop is very rich. That makes her leery of him. His family owns a chain of hotels but he admits he does not want to follow his father's footsteps. Is he using Caymen? Seeing how the other half lives? <br>Why has he never watched the Shining?!?!! That's my burning question.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/X4UFS3P" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1544483403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544483403" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544483403?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=young-adult-contemporary">young-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=rom-com">rom-com</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544483403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6374747186150298520"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Feelings can be the most costly thing in the universe."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>The cover and the premise of this book somewhat deceived me. Ha! Yes, it was cute and adorable. Funny, even. But that's not just about it. My expectations were different. <br/><br/><b>Caymen Meyers</b> is a teenage girl who works for her mom's doll store. One day a rich and cute guy named <b>Xander Spence</b> comes over to their store to buy a doll for her grandma. Because he obviously has the air of wealth, Caymen sees him as just another one of those</span>
  <span id="freeText6374747186150298520" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Feelings can be the most costly thing in the universe."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The cover and the premise of this book somewhat deceived me. Ha! Yes, it was cute and adorable. Funny, even. But that's not just about it. My expectations were different. <br><br><b>Caymen Meyers</b> is a teenage girl who works for her mom's doll store. One day a rich and cute guy named <b>Xander Spence</b> comes over to their store to buy a doll for her grandma. Because he obviously has the air of wealth, Caymen sees him as just another one of those spoiled, rich kids who treat poor people differently. Which turns out wrong. As they begin to form friendship, Caymen slowly warms up to him and realizes that he's completely different from what she expected to be like.<br><br>What I loved about this book was the <b>humor</b>. Nothing else. The rest was a let-down. First, I really thought Caymen was a likeable character but she's not. She's hilarious but her sarcasm and dry humor are a total turn-off. Aside from that, I was also a bit bothered by the way she perceives her family's social and financial status. She keeps pointing out that they are poor but if we take a closer look, they're actually average because they can pay the bills, they can eat three (or more times) a day, AND they even have a business for chrissake! In a way, it was so lame and pathetic to make it a big deal and to even view the rich people as haughty and superior. <br><br>My huge problem in this book was also the romantic aspect. I couldn't find myself swooning over the characters. Their interactions seem pointless and insignificant. Also, while I loved Xander's character, I find him unbeliveable. Seriously, he's too rich to be true! And whoa, a guy who owns hundreds of hotels and who is often featured in gossip magazines would be interested with a plain girl? Isn't it too cliche and Cinderella-ish? In my opinion.<br><br>So, yes. It didn't work out for me. Maybe if I read this book years ago when I was still in my teenage years, I would've appreciated it, because why not? It's cuteness overload! But then stories like these rarely amaze me these days, so yeah.<br><br>Rating:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447324535i/16987052.jpg" width="200" height="45" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445993261i/16730770.jpg" width="200" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6374747186150298520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I survived the ordeal…<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Thank you very much for allowing me to…what the hell are you wearing?<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> I came in costume.<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Dressed as what? It looks like the 70s threw up on you.<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Elton John. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> You came to an interview for a book review that <i>you</i> requested dressed as-. You know what, why don’t we just get this over with? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> *hums the opening bars to Rocket Man*<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> What made you want to pick up <i>The Distance Between Us</i> instead of one of the 80 ARCs that you probably should have read instead? *mutters* if you were a responsible adult…<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> I blame <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572231405" rel="nofollow noopener">Komal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622736552" rel="nofollow noopener">Cecile</a><br /><br /><b>PR:</b> So, it’s not your fault? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Nope! I had no choice. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> *mutters* of course not…<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Plus, have you seen this cover? Look at it. <i>Look. At. It.</i><br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Yes. I see that. Did you really need to just hit me in the face with the book though? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> *whispers* It’s okay precious, the mean man doesn’t understand. What’s that? No, I’d never let him take you away from mommy. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Are you on drugs right now? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> What? No. Why would you ask that?<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> *mutters* no reason…<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Do you have some sort of speech impediment? <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> No I don’t have- *takes deep breath* This is getting off topic, why don’t you tell me what you expected going into this book. <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Words<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> *grinds teeth* I meant how did you <i>feel</i>? Were you nervous because in the past you haven’t had the best track record with books that everyone else loved? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> That’s such a strange turn of phrase; track record. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Just answer the goddamn question! <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Wow, <i>someone’s</i> manstrating. Jeez, yes, I was nervous. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> And after reading the book? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Why would I still be nervous? I’ve read it. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> *bites out* What were your feelings upon completion of the book? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Oh, happy ones. <br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Care to elaborate?<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Well, I suppose there’s a lyric that can best sum up how I felt. Ahem! <i> “It was Saturday late, have you seen my mates, can you tell me when the boys get here? Well, it's seven o'clock and I want to rock and get a belly full of beer.”</i><br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Really? Saturday Night’s Alright for Fighting? <br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Hey! You’ve heard of it! One of my best if I do say so my-<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> That’s it! *spikes pen*<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> What are you-<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> *throws chair*<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> Hey, where are you-<br /><br /><b>PR:</b> Fuck this shit, I quit!<br /><br /><b>LC:</b> What the hell was that guy’s problem? <br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11257406321698640219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_505890168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/505890168" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/505890168?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062235664" href="/book/show/17251018-the-distance-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=true-5-starers">true-5-starers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=swoony-boys">swoony-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=stand-alone-books">stand-alone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=on-my-real-shelves">on-my-real-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=harper-teen">harper-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505890168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3737865256113195109"><i>Pretty in Pink meets Pride and Prejudice.</i> That's the best explanation of this book I've seen so far. <br/><br/>Kasie West has done it again... I thought I was a fan of her writing after I read Pivot Point. After reading The Distance Between Us... I may have escalated to fangirl. <br/><br/><a href='http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/anigif_enhanced-buzz-4736-1360291424-7_zps31c6f0c2.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/612165.gif' alt=' photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-4736-1360291424-7_zps31c6f0c2.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This book made me all kinds of happy. First reason... that cover. I love love it. <br/><br/>Caymen Meyers lives with her single mother and learned early on that the rich are very different than her. Working the register at her mother's </span>
  <span id="freeText3737865256113195109" style="display:none"><i>Pretty in Pink meets Pride and Prejudice.</i> That's the best explanation of this book I've seen so far. <br><br>Kasie West has done it again... I thought I was a fan of her writing after I read Pivot Point. After reading The Distance Between Us... I may have escalated to fangirl. <br><br><a href="http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/anigif_enhanced-buzz-4736-1360291424-7_zps31c6f0c2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/612165.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-4736-1360291424-7_zps31c6f0c2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book made me all kinds of happy. First reason... that cover. I love love it. <br><br>Caymen Meyers lives with her single mother and learned early on that the rich are very different than her. Working the register at her mother's doll shop, she's encountered her fair share of them and her mom hasn't exactly been secretive about her feelings toward them. <br><br>Then Xander Spence enters the store. <br><br>He's tall, gorgeous and obviously rich. From the first 'beckon' the evolution of their friendship hooked me. <br><br>I'm not going to tell as much about the story itself because I'm afraid I might give something important away... instead I'm going to tell you about what I loved most - the characters. <br><br>From the first chapter, West had me hooked. I want Caymen as a best friend. I think that we would hit it off. Her sarcasm and dry humor made her completely likable and relatable. <br><br><i>"Is that your subtle way of saying you missed me last week?"<br><br>"I've missed my hot chocolate. I just think of you as the guy who brings it to me. Sometimes I forget your name and call you hot chocolate guy."</i><br><br>Where she is in her life made me want to hug her. She has one friend in her life and almost all her time is spent working in the shop. She shoulders so much for a 17 year old, that it's hard not to feel a bit of anger towards her mother. <br><br>Xander.... <br><br><a href="http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/anigif_enhanced-buzz-28338-1360290338-2_zps2aea24d9.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386891ra/746565.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-28338-1360290338-2_zps2aea24d9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The boy made my top five swoony boy list. I don't know what exactly it was about him... maybe it was that he didn't take himself too seriously even though he is who he is, and he really truly cares about Caymen that made him so lovely. I don't know, but he totally won me over. He can have the first sip of ALL my drinks... I'm totally okay with this. <br><br>Now the two of them together had me smiling like a fool. Watching them get to know each other and learn about each other and fall for each other was the best part of this book for me. <br><br><i>Xander opens the compartment above my knees and takes out a pair of leather gloves. As he pulls them on I can't help but laugh.<br><br>"What?"<br><br>"You have driving gloves."<br><br>"And?"<br><br>"And it's funny."<br><br>"Funny adorable?"<br><br>I shake my head. "If you say so."</i><br><br>Cayman soon finds out that Xander is being groomed to take over his father's hotel business but he feels like he's being forced into it and Caymen isn't entirely sure what she wants to do after graduation but she thinks it will be helping her mom in the store even though that's the last thing she wants. Xander is convinced that they have the same problem going on in their lives ... they just don't know what's next, but they can work together to try and find out what exactly they should be doing with their lives by creating 'career days' for each other. <br><br>Of course everything isn't easy and their circumstances seem to make things complicated but not in the way you might think, and she quickly learns that his family isn't made up of the horrible people that she's been led to believe.<br><br>Along the way, Caymen finds out that some of the things she's been led to believe aren't exactly true and her world is turned upside down. <br><br>If you're looking for a sweet contemporary with some wonderfully developed characters then you must pick up The Distance Between Us when it comes out in July! I know I'll be buying a copy for my bookshelf.<br><br>After loving both Pivot Point and The Distance Between Us, Kasie West is now on my auto-buy list.<br><br>P.S. - Stacee... Xander is mine!! LOL :) <br><br><a href="http://s757.photobucket.com/user/jaimearkin/media/9acd0cc9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380380119i/736750.jpg" alt=" photo 9acd0cc9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This review can be found on my blog, Fic Fare: <br><a href="http://fictionfare.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380223306ra/681029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> </span>

<div id="review_1247060738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247060738" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247060738?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247060738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10783534447215105783"><b>REREAD</b><br/><br/>I enjoyed it even more the second time around. The things that bothered me the first time I read it were no longer an issue to me. <b>Xander</b> has become more adorable and pleasing in my eyes while <b>Caymen</b>’s sarcasm is clearly topnotch. I have completely forgotten about Mason though. I couldn’t even remember that there was another guy and a potential love interest at that in the story. The beckoning gesture, I still vividly remember though. Lol! This is why rereading is the best. So I guess my o</span>
  <span id="freeText10783534447215105783" style="display:none"><b>REREAD</b><br><br>I enjoyed it even more the second time around. The things that bothered me the first time I read it were no longer an issue to me. <b>Xander</b> has become more adorable and pleasing in my eyes while <b>Caymen</b>’s sarcasm is clearly topnotch. I have completely forgotten about Mason though. I couldn’t even remember that there was another guy and a potential love interest at that in the story. The beckoning gesture, I still vividly remember though. Lol! This is why rereading is the best. So I guess my old review still holds true except that this time, I liked it even more. Of course, I read it in one sitting. <br>_ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ <br>ORIGINAL REVIEW WRITTEN APRIL 7, 2015<br><br><b> 3.90 stars </b><br><br>[In deep, scary male voice] <br><br><b> A GRAVEYARD </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428470055ra/14429401.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> CREEPY PORCELAIN DOLLS </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428469724ra/14429336.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> A DEAD BODY being prepped for funeral </b>…<br><br>*This is only a mock-up of a dead body as it would be too harsh to post an image of a real one*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428469724i/14429337.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[coughs back to normal female voice]<br><br><b> TRUST ME, THIS IS A ROMANTIC YA STORY. Lol! </b><br><br>Despite the odd morbid elements as mentioned in the intro, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (there actually was a cheesy mud fight scene at the grave, lol!^^) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I know now I can rely on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a> for fluffy, light reads. Just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18298225.On_the_Fence" title="On the Fence by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Fence</a>, this has short chapters, enjoyable characters, cozy beach town setting and a fun, witty, sarcastic heroine and a too beautiful hero. (Personally though, I still prefer On the Fence just a tad more. )<br><br>Admittedly, instead of just completely enjoying myself with this book, I found myself battling with several “issues” like the over pushed characterization and themes. <br><br>I totally get it that this is about overcoming economic/social status distance for love (actually the “distance” in the title made me think this was about geographical distance, but I was wrong. I guess I was hoping it was that but never mind. Lol.) But in so many occasions, I felt like the premise is yelling at me way too much. <br><br>Just to give you a peek at the story- Caymen (the lead female) is poor (sorry there’s no other simpler way to say it when the character herself keeps reminding you that) while Alexander (the lead male) is rich and I’m pretty sure you know what comes next taking to account that this is a YA romance. <br><br>What just bothers me is the lack of subtlety in putting across the purpose of the story- Caymen for example keeps going on and on about how small her house is every time she’s at home and there are a lot of times she’s at home. Alexander on the other hand is unrealistically soooooo rich (at least to me). He has a personal plane, a music studio, more than three sports cars, is about to inherit 50 hotels, I mean GAH!!!! STOP!!! Rub it in much??? (or maybe I just haven’t met a filthy rich person ever in my life).<br><br>Also, I know that when Alex said the following line, it’s supposed to make me swoon…<br> <br> <b> <i> "You are poor and I still like you." </i></b>  <br><br>…but the only reaction it got from me is…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407269840ra/10666321.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> Sorry about the rant. I just had to let it out. ^^</b><br><br>I know I may have sneezed out a lot of negatives but I still enjoyed reading the story. I liked the little conflicts in the almost linear but in a pleasant way kind of plot and I like how these conflicts were resolved. I also like the atmosphere of friendship and family that prevailed in the story and I definitely like the smooth flow of events and of course, the happy ending. <br><br>So, are you suffering from a terrible disease called book slump or just looking for a light, enjoyable read? I SO recommend this.^^</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10783534447215105783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1823080484" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1823080484" />
    <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely"><img alt="Frankie Lovely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493240668p2/61971658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823080484?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frankie Lovely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frankie Lovely" href="/user/show/61971658-frankie-lovely">Frankie Lovely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823080484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15224949771375175717"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I just want to give a warning that .. this review was written after consuming copious amounts of Jack Daniels … so I apologize in advance if it make NO SENSE! <br/><br/>This book was not the most horrific thing I have ever read … so there is that. I honestly enjoyed it … to an extent. But it was not without it’s problems.<br/><br/>This was my second attempt at a Kasie West book and I have to say … I was mildly disappointed yet again. On the one hand, I enjoyed this book a lot more than I enjoyed By Your Si</span>
  <span id="freeText15224949771375175717" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />I just want to give a warning that .. this review was written after consuming copious amounts of Jack Daniels … so I apologize in advance if it make NO SENSE! <br /><br />This book was not the most horrific thing I have ever read … so there is that. I honestly enjoyed it … to an extent. But it was not without it’s problems.<br /><br />This was my second attempt at a Kasie West book and I have to say … I was mildly disappointed yet again. On the one hand, I enjoyed this book a lot more than I enjoyed By Your Side (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826895399?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">See Review HERE</a>) but I did not LOVE this book by any stretch of the imagination. It was cute … I guess. <br /><br /><b>What I Liked</b><br /><br />The relationship building was nice and slow but not boring or without merit, and I didn’t want to stab the MC in the eye. So all in all I count that as a moderate win.<br /><br />I enjoyed Xander's character a lot ... he was precious and honestly deserves better ... like I don't see what it was that attracted him to Caymen ... the romance makes no since because he has no reason to fall for her?<br /><br /><b>What I did not like</b><br /><br />I recently ranted about how OVER the “rich people are the devil” trope I keep seeing and BAM … in my fucking FACE with it … oh fucking awesome!<br /><br />On the one hand … this book felt more genuine than my last Kasie West attempt with By Your Side … but on the other hand … this book threw DOWN with the “rich people suck” trope. I mean honestly, that’s really all this book was … a poor girl hating on rich boy because rich people suck! AMIRIGHT? <br /><br />The MC couldn't have been more clear in her disdain for rich people if she tried … like seriously! This concept was literally the ONLY strife between these two! He’s rich and I'm now .. meh let me cry about it for 300+ pages! Yep … that’s the book … the whole book!<br /><br />I really did not like Caymen ... I didn't hate her ... but I would not be her friend IRL like ever. She seems like she might be an okay human ... but Kasie West failed to explain to me WHY Caymen is a cool girl and worthy of Xander's affections. The romance seemed ones sided because of this. Xander was all in from the moment he decided "this is the girl" but like ... why? What building blocks were in place to make him feel this way? I can see why Caymen would like him ... but she was the reluctant one. I just need more foundation!!<br /><br />Again, I didn’t hate this book … but anytime you repeat something too much as an author … it becomes distracting AF! I could have done with a little less rich shaming and been happy. That’s all … that’s not too much to ask I think ...<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion</b><br /><br />Not terrible .. not great. Enjoyable but nothing to light a torch over. I am going to give West another try because I did enjoy thing one more than my first West read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15224949771375175717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_989212873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989212873" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/989212873?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer989212873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10408637763853479900">This book is just straight-up really bad.<br/><br/>Like, you know how there are sometimes movies that are just objectively not good? I’m talking zero-percent on Rotten Tomatoes/has become a cult classic for how bad it is levels of awful. <br/><br/>It is fun to watch that type of movie and be like wow, look how bad this is! But there’s not really an equivalent to that phenomenon in books.<br/><br/>This little number comes pretty close to that. Except it doesn’t always land the “fun” part. But it is very very very bad and also</span>
  <span id="freeText10408637763853479900" style="display:none">This book is just straight-up really bad.<br /><br />Like, you know how there are sometimes movies that are just objectively not good? I’m talking zero-percent on Rotten Tomatoes/has become a cult classic for how bad it is levels of awful. <br /><br />It is fun to watch that type of movie and be like wow, look how bad this is! But there’s not really an equivalent to that phenomenon in books.<br /><br />This little number comes pretty close to that. Except it doesn’t always land the “fun” part. But it is very very very bad and also dumb. It’s so dumb I reached out to scientists and had my number of brain cells tracked just so I could confirm to you all that it decreased significantly after I read this book.<br /><br />I don’t even know how to convey just how bad this is. It’s like...you need to read it to understand. Here are some things that happen that may help your comprehension:<br /><br />- The love interest’s credit card has the name “Xander Spence” on it, which is truly a shock considering no credit card on earth has a nickname on it and his birth certificate sure as sh*t doesn’t say his legal given name is “Xander”<br />- Xander wears driving gloves, as if that is something a normal twenty-first century adolescent does<br />- Our main character, Caymen (because lol of course) hears that her mother is going to have an ultrasound, and she, a near-adult female of (allegedly) sound mind, does not know what an ultrasound is<br />- Caymen says, “We should toilet paper someone’s house,” and the response is, “Yes. We should TP someone’s house.” You know. How normal humans talk.<br />- We get some fresh fresh not like other girls trope: Xander says, “You’re different, Caymen.” Caymen: “Different than what?” Xander: “Than any other girl I’ve met.” Because of course!<br />- But wait, there’s more: “I hope I'm not turning into <i>that</i> girl, the one who daydreams about a guy she can never have.” Ah, yes, the classic girls-come-in-types conundrum!<br />- Caymen picks up Xander’s phone when the girl she believes he is dating is calling. I don’t know why. I have no explanation for this.<br />- Caymen is such a f*cking stupid name. Not even Cayman. I’m sorry, I just had to say that.<br />- There’s a goddamn love triangle in this, as if things could get any worse.<br />- Also emotional cheating, because things actually CAN get worse. Caymen thought they were cheating, but it’s actually fine because they weren’t! Cool!<br />- Luckily, Caymen has the perfect justification for this behavior: “She probably can't make him laugh.” Phew! Sounds like the girl deserves to be cheated on! She hypothetically might not be as funny as you in your own imagination? A monster!<br />- Fun little tidbits of writing like: “Is Scarlett going because I don’t know if I can put up with her this year?”<br />- And: “The bartender points to the door off to the side from the stage when Skye gives him the questioning shoulder raise.” Ah, yes, the good ol’ questioning shoulder raise!<br />- Pretty sure someone has the Chinese symbol for acceptance tattooed or some sh*t, which just...kill me<br />- There’s my FAVORITE indication of very bad writing: the insta-friendship. Every time a girl pops up in a contemporary only to become the immediate BFF of our protagonist it reminds me of a Justin Bieber fanfiction from 2010 in which the love interest becomes best friends with Demi Lovato and Selena Gomez seconds after encountering them. Good times. Very bad writing.<br /><br />Anyway. Caymen sucks and is mean and boring and annoying and stupid and Xander is the most spoiled weird annoying dumb rich kid of all time so they so totally deserve each other.<br /><br />And this book is bad.<br /><br />Bottom line: the last thing I expected was for this book to be evidence of Kasie West improving over the years, but here we are.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10408637763853479900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2290577262761446542" style="display:none">AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOH MY GAWD!!!!!<br><br><b>Guess who's my new book boyfriend!<br>Guess!!!<br>I bet you can't guess correctly.<br>IT'S ROBERT!!<br>Ha! <br>Just kidding!<br>It's Xander. Of course it's Xander! Who else could it possibly be? The boy is simply <i>beyond</i> wonderful!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477592294ra/20969794.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a beautiful book about a beautiful budding relationship between two beautiful people!<br>(Ale)Xander and Caymen.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484179886ra/21690709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guys I fangirled SO HARD! <br>I literally finished this in one sitting. <br>ONE SITTING!<br>AND I SHOULD HAVE BEEN STUDYING DURING THOSE HOURS, BUT INSTEAD, I STARTED AND FINISHED A BOOK!<br>I wasn't intending on finishing, but I literally could not stop.<br>I couldn't tear my eyes away from the page!<br>Xander is who I want. I want a guy exactly like Xander! Why can I not find a guy like Xander?<br><b>It seems like in all these book worlds there are high populations of Xanders. Why can't my world by populated by Xanders?<br>Instead, my crappy world is populated by asshole Roberts and too touchy Masons.<i>WHY</i> is there no perfect balance? Why are there like zero chivalrous guys in my world? I would happily jump into a book world any day.<br><br>There needs to be like a goblin black market of authors who can literally bring these wonderful book men into real life. I would sell my soul for a Dimitri or a Xander.<br>Scientists: get on this, stat!!!!</b><br><br>Caymen is so awesome!!! I can't even!<br>A lot of times, I'll love a chick lit because the guy is so wonderful, but in this one not only did Xander have my heart, but Caymen did as well.<br>Her sarcasm is <b>through the roof</b> hilarious! She's my new model.<br>Honestly I'm so sarcastic, I thought I was the Queen of Sarcasm.<br>But no way.<br>Caymen holds that title by a landslide. There is absolutely no competition.<br><br><b>

He opens the bag, takes out a muffin, and hands it to me. The top glistens with sprinkled sugar. "Really?"<br>I gently unwrap it. "No.” <br>
</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Except maybe for her grandfather, who is FABULOUS by the way.<br><br><b>

    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/620863960?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer620863960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer79999173594573923"><b>This book is so entirely STUFFED with sarcasm. I feel connected on a spiritual level.</b> I do. It's like this book is <i>mine</i>. I am Caymen. Minus, you know, the creepy doll shop and the freakishly sweet boyfriend. BUT I GOT THE SARCASM DOWN PAT. Go me. <i>Anyway</i>. We really need to talk about this book. <b>For starters: I loved it.</b> I don't even usually like fluffy contemporaries, but I loved this one a lot. It really ought to be 5-stars, I KNOW it does...but that ending? It was disappointing on so so many le</span>
  <span id="freeText79999173594573923" style="display:none"><b>This book is so entirely STUFFED with sarcasm. I feel connected on a spiritual level.</b> I do. It's like this book is <i>mine</i>. I am Caymen. Minus, you know, the creepy doll shop and the freakishly sweet boyfriend. BUT I GOT THE SARCASM DOWN PAT. Go me. <i>Anyway</i>. We really need to talk about this book. <b>For starters: I loved it.</b> I don't even usually like fluffy contemporaries, but I loved this one a lot. It really ought to be 5-stars, I KNOW it does...but that ending? It was disappointing on so so many levels. SO I'M GONNA WRITE A LIST. The good, the bad, and the ugly. But all you really need to know is: you need this sarcastically adorable book in your life ASAP. <br /><br /><b>STUFF I FREAKING LOVED TO PIECES. JUST GIVE ME ROOM. I NEED TO FLAIL:</b><br />I'm an estastic flailer too, by the way. <br /><br /><b>+ Sarcasm.</b> I read about a lot of irritatingly sarcastic teens, but this is DIFFERENT. For starters, it's the <i>best</i> strain of sarcasm. It's very self-deprecating or based on surroundings. Caymen doesn't take the mickey out of anyone. She doesn't act "woe is me". She just says the opposite to everything and is 1000% endearing because of it. She's so quick! And the humour is written wonderfully. The author doesn't pause to "explain" when Caymen's being sarcastic...and believe me, I read a TON of books where the author feels the need to explain. Drives. me. bonkers. So this?! THIS IS JUST PERFECT. I laughed out loud so so much.<br /><blockquote>“Note to self: Caymen is very good at sarcasm.”<br />“If you’re recording notes for an official record, I’d like the word ‘very’ stricken and replaced with ‘exceptionally.” </blockquote><br /><b> + Caymen and Xander are just adorably shippable.</b> They are literally PERFECT for each other. He's sweet, she's snarky. Like what more could I possibly want?!<br /><b> + Also: such epic character development.</b> It's definitely a slow-burn romance. They become friends <i>first</i>, which is what I love to read. And they change and grow throughout the story. HUZZAH. <br /><b> + The writing is just excellent.</b> It's vivid, but not drowningly so. It adds in plenty of details, there's delicious food, and plenty of settings. And it deals with the themes of "what should I do with my life" which is HUGE when you're facing the end of highschool. (I totally related to Caymen's feelings, and retable books are THE BEST.) I got all the feels and all the fuzzies and I totally didn't want to put this book down. <br /><br />okay...so now for the <i>not</i> so hot stuff. And seriously this is just like 99% to do with the last few chapters of the book! Which really bugs me because I was going to rate this 5-stars and then....well...let me explain. <br /><br /><b>STUFF THAT BROKE MY HEART BECAUSE IT JUST DIDN'T WORK FOR ME AT ALL:</b><br />No, I'm not dramatic. Shush and read. <br /><br /><b> + The ending wraps up like the neatest birthday present in the world. </b> No, and no. I'm not an "unhappy ending" lover, but I do like a shred of realism. This book is SO VERY UNREALISTIC at the end that it kind of spoiled the realistic and adorable romance. The book seems to bypass anything and everything awkward a to arrive at a cosy snuggle. Huh. I feel absolutely cheated. For instance, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there was such potential for a messy love-triangle since Caymen was leading Mason on while being zero percent interested in him. But that sort of just shrugged away and Mason faded when Caymen finally decided she did, indeed, like Xander. And, well, let's bring in the estranged grandparents to clean up the debts and sort everything up! HOW ABOUT NO. There wasn't even a shred of awkwardness, they just meshed the grandparents in like they'd lost their daughter...not being living like 4 hours away from her for the last seventeen years. Apparently THEY threw Caymen's mum out the door?? But there's no shred of past animosity now. Oh no. Everyone suddenly LURVES each other. But I can't understand why they lived so close! If you want to ditch your parents, don't you run to the other side of the country? Or at least state?!! Don't get me wrong: I love the grandparents. I just felt it was so unrealistic. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b> + The ending was really rushed too.</b> After so much build up and intrigue and questions, I just felt like I got EVERYTHING dumped on me in a few pages. It was <i>rush rush rush</i> and that startled me and left a sour taste in my mouth. COME ON. I wanted blueberry muffins and hot chocolate, yes, but I wanted to <i>chew</i> not gulp.<br /><b> + While I felt the book had a lot of "follow your dreams" themes in it...I think it kind of faceplanted towards the end.</b> This bit is basically a spoiler, so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I felt it was incredibly unfair that Caymen could follow her dreams, but Xander couldn't. He was "good at" being in charge of hotels, so therefore that was his calling?! No way! You can be good at things and not be passionate about them. I was so so frustrated that this was the climax! Why shouldn't Xander discover something new??? After all, on the "career days", he gave Caymen the opportunities of a LIFE TIME and she made him dig a grave. So. Yeah. Naturally he didn't find something else he loved. This stinks a bit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><b>Don't get me wrong: I FREAKING LOVED THIS BOOK.</b> I surprise myself, since I'm so twitchy toward contemporaries. There were definitely a bunch of things that spoiled the ending...buuuut...I still have infinite love for it from the first 90%. I ship Xander and Caymen quite furiously. This was also my first Kasie West book...AND I WANT MORE ASAP.</span>
  <a data-text-id="79999173594573923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1117920336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117920336" />
    <a title="Marnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33816538-marnie"><img alt="Marnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560300852p2/33816538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1117920336?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marnie" href="/user/show/33816538-marnie">Marnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1117920336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17389028388084493175">Everyone, it's official. <b>I am in love with Kasie West's writing</b>.<br/><br/>This is probably one of the cutest contemporary books I've read all year. Okay, I didn't love it as much as I loved The Fill-In Boyfriend, but that doesn't stop it from being up there! <br/><br/>The story revolves around a girl named Caymen. Caymen doesn't exactly come from the richest of families, so she does all that she can to help her mother out, which includes working...at a doll store. Let's just say, this isn't Caymen's passion in life</span>
  <span id="freeText17389028388084493175" style="display:none">Everyone, it's official. <b>I am in love with Kasie West's writing</b>.<br /><br />This is probably one of the cutest contemporary books I've read all year. Okay, I didn't love it as much as I loved The Fill-In Boyfriend, but that doesn't stop it from being up there! <br /><br />The story revolves around a girl named Caymen. Caymen doesn't exactly come from the richest of families, so she does all that she can to help her mother out, which includes working...at a doll store. Let's just say, this isn't Caymen's passion in life, rather than her mothers. Anyway, one day Caymen is working her usual shift, and an obnoxiously rich boy enters the store. He beckons her over for help in the rudest way possible, which only confirms Caymen's suspicion of obnoxious rich kid. <b>This is where it all begins...</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>His eyes are so intense I want to look away...or never look away. I can’t decide.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />From the start, it was clear Caymen was going to fall head-over-heels for Xander. Although she doesn't have the greatest first impression of him, it's clear after their first meeting (date? hang-out sesh? altercation? what am I supposed to call it?) that they just understand each other on a different level. I was going to say Xander could beckon me over any day, but I will refrain myself from saying something so outrageous! Seriously though, Caymen was a complete sucker for Xander! It's not as if he did much wrong, but c'mon, the man could murder someone and she'd still fall for his hard-to-come-by smile.<br /><br />This book is literally full of sarcasm, AKA, <i>my forte</i>. Caymen's dry humour honestly keeps the story alive. Without it, this book would be just another cheese-fest. And I mean cheese-fest.<br /><br />If you're not into cliché romances, where boy tells girl that she's not like other girls, look away now, <b>because that literally happens in this book</b>. Now, I'm a sucker for all things love, but even this was just too much. I THOUGHT WE STOPPED USING THAT LINE IN 1990!<br /><br />Towards the end of the book, I did feel like Xander's wealth was mentioned on every other page! Like ... We get it ... He's a good person whilst simultaneously being insanely rich. We now know not to judge books by their covers. Hooray! <br /><br />Although I liked the ending, I did feel like it was completely rushed. I felt like we hardly saw Caymen and Xander as a couple, if you know what I mean? I definitely did not get enough closure, and would <i>love</i> a second book. Or even novella. I want to see her relationship with Xander &amp; her grandparents bloom, and perhaps a reconnection with her father? Also, maybe reading from Xander's perspective would be kind of cool. I mean, I do want to know if that asshole Robert really was calling Caymen a stray. He was the worst. <br /><br />This book had the perfect amount of banter, honestly. I feel like Caymen's sarcasm eventually reached Xander, and although he was the serious one at times, he began to gain his own sense of dry humour. Not to mention the fact that he fully appreciated Caymen's sense of humour! Where can I find myself a man like that!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“So Caymen..."<br />"So, Xander..."<br />"Like the islands."<br />"What?"<br />"Your name. Caymen. Like the Cayman Islands. Is that your mom's favourite place to visit or something?"<br />"No, it's her third favourite place. I have an older brother named Paris and an older sister named Sydney."<br />"Wow." He opens the bag, takes out a muffin, and hands it to me. The top glistens with sprinkled sugar. "Really?"<br />I gently unwrap it. "No.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I'm beginning to recognise Kasie West's knack for unusual names, and <b>I love it</b>. Seriously, what a unique way to bring a little bit of originality to the story! <br /><br />One of my favourite parts of the story, was Xander and Caymen's ritual with the hot chocolate. For some strange reason, I found it so insanely adorable that Xander taking a sip out of Caymen's drink became their habit. Their thing, if you will. Overall, this book was just the cutest, and I hope to find someone that loves me the way that Xander loves Caymen. Or vice versa, because seriously, this is a couple that love each other with all they've got. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Is that your subtle way of saying you missed me last week?"<br /><br />"I've missed my hot chocolate. I just think of you as the guy who brings it to me. Sometimes I forget your name and call you hot chocolate guy.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="17389028388084493175" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
