<div id="review_1836113694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836113694" />
    <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu"><img alt="Ramona Popescu " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594649997p2/33526516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836113694?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona Popescu " href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu">Ramona Popescu </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33526516-ramona-popescu?shelf=read-but-forgotten">read-but-forgotten</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33526516-ramona-popescu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836113694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10750193169634891920">This is my first Kasie West book, but sincerely, it wasn't for me at all...<br/>I won't lose your time very much, because I don't have a lot to say.. read the book and see it for yourself.<br/><br/>Caymen is your average girl next door, living with her mother in an apartment right on top of their doll shop. Yes, she sells dolls, but deep inside she is not satisfied with this life, wanting to do other things, but right in this moment, she doesn't have a certain answer to her future. She chooses the save way mom</span>
  <span id="freeText10750193169634891920" style="display:none">This is my first Kasie West book, but sincerely, it wasn't for me at all...<br>I won't lose your time very much, because I don't have a lot to say.. read the book and see it for yourself.<br><br>Caymen is your average girl next door, living with her mother in an apartment right on top of their doll shop. Yes, she sells dolls, but deep inside she is not satisfied with this life, wanting to do other things, but right in this moment, she doesn't have a certain answer to her future. She chooses the save way momentarily, and really refuses to think about it. She meets Xander, a rich nephew of one of her best clients and of course they immediately chick things off. He is young, rich, but with a lot of burdens to bare, having a not very patient and loving family, who aspect a lot for him. They became good friends, but it is clear that something will go on between them.<br><br>This kind of sums up the plot, and although it started really promising, I soon realised that I won't obtain nothing from this book. This 2 stars are only for the heroine here, because she was a different type of girl. That sarcasm and irony were so well built and in this way I could see the writer's talent. She really has potential, but somewhere down the road, the story was flat and without anything major happening. She could have explored more in depth this characters, but stop at a certain point.<br><br>Xander had nothing special, just an average boy who was not happy with his life, despite having everything in it. He didn't fit, he didn't have a clue where to fit, and in a way considered Caymen his equal because they were both disorientated and sad. But from my POV they didn't had chemistry and I couldn't connect with their love story, because I couldn't pin point the moment when they clicked..<br><br>The story was flat. There were some pretty interesting moments when the writer could have added drama or a spark, but she didn't.. She preferred the old way, the safe one and the outcome was left incomplete and unsatisfying. It was boring some times and I waited and waited for something to happen, but it didn't. I've read similar books, but after finishing them I was left with a message, a lesson. But here, as I said, I think things were left hanging and without any conclusion.<br><br>Sorry for the 2 stars, but I had no choice.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479123324i/21149668._SX540_.png" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more reviews please check <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com">https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="10750193169634891920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_584553652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584553652" />
    <a title="Ellis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10165983-ellis"><img alt="Ellis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374415848p2/10165983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584553652?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellis" href="/user/show/10165983-ellis">Ellis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=let-s-have-beautiful-cover-babies">let-s-have-beautiful-cover-babies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=please-be-my-friend-too">please-be-my-friend-too</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=sexy-times">sexy-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=boss-heroine">boss-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=disappointing-execution">disappointing-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=i-am-not-amused">i-am-not-amused</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=in-my-possession">in-my-possession</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10165983-ellis?shelf=who-needs-sleep-anyway">who-needs-sleep-anyway</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584553652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14905025504308170077">The verdict: 3.75 stars.<br/><br/>Because I remain professional at all times, I should say that I'm docking a quarter star because I struggled a bit with the beginning and an entire star because I had a whole set of problems with the end. However, the official reason is and will always be:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416780i/823536._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Eeeerrrhh ... It's just ... I can't ... HUH?!<br/><br/><br/>I'm legitimately concerned about this. There's a reason it's called "warme chocolademelk" (hot chocolate milk) in Dutch. As a virtual ambassador for the land of chocolate, I f</span>
  <span id="freeText14905025504308170077" style="display:none">The verdict: 3.75 stars.<br><br>Because I remain professional at all times, I should say that I'm docking a quarter star because I struggled a bit with the beginning and an entire star because I had a whole set of problems with the end. However, the official reason is and will always be:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416780i/823536._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eeeerrrhh ... It's just ... I can't ... HUH?!<br><br><br>I'm legitimately concerned about this. There's a reason it's called "warme chocolademelk" (hot chocolate milk) in Dutch. As a virtual ambassador for the land of chocolate, I feel it is my duty to rectify this situation, because this is just WRONG. <br><br><b>How to make delicious hot chocolate</b>:<br><br><u>For 1-2 cup(s)<br><br>1. Ingredients</u><br><br>- 200 ml milk<br>- 1 spoon of cocoa powder (or a few pieces of dark chocolate if you're really hardcore)<br><br><u>2. Preparation</u><br><br>- Pour the milk in a steel pan. <br>(<i>Students and other laid-back people: it's acceptable to just put the cup in the microwave. It doesn't take away from the taste. However, <u>water</u> does.</i>)<br>- Heat the milk until right before it starts bubbling and rising.<br>(<i>This is tricky, but you'll quickly get the hang of it.</i>)<br>- Add the cocoa powder or chocolat. <br>- Stir until you have a smooth mixture.<br>- Whipped cream and other toppings are optional.<br>- Enjoy the chocolatey goodness and read the rest of this review.<br><br><br>So that was the semi-original part of my review. For the rest, I think I have remarks very similar to those other reviewers who really liked this book made. I am one of those people who says: "I read books for the characters.", which becomes more important when you read contemporary. I generally struggle with this genre. Maybe I'm just an escapist reader. I need the high stakes of fantasy and the imagination of a world completely foreign to ours. However, this doesn't mean I can't enjoy stories like <i>The Distance Between Us</i>, although I do think West's <i>Pivot Point</i> series might be a better fit for me.<br><br>Caymen is pure brilliance. I often felt for her and she made me laugh almost every time she opened her mouth or, you know, took a step or a breath or something. Overall, I'm really impressed with the female characters in this book. Skye is a wonderful best friend, which is something I so often miss in the genres I just declared to be my favourites. From the few (non-NA) contemporaries I have read so far, female friendships have been handled very well, which makes me very, very happy. I find this important.<br><br>The two characters I'm really conflicted about are Caymen's mother, Susan, and the love interest, Xander. I'll get to Susan in a bit, because her character ties in with the major problem I have with this book (besided the chocolate milk debacle, of course), which is the unsatisfactory resolution to the class issues. <br><br>So, Xander. This guy just didn't do it for me. He was nice enough and he seemed to make Caymen genuinely happy, which is something I can only root for, because YAY CAYMEN! Their chemistry was definitely there and their conversations and banter were laughs and feels and giggles and snorts all wrapped in one big ball of <i>OMG I'm so happy for you, Caymen!</i> <br><br>However, the thing that irked me about Xander is that he's so entitled and clueless about his privilege. I don't like that he had to be the richest of the rich, especially with how things played out with Caymen's family. What was even the point of all that if you're going that route anyway? Yes, Xander genuinely cares for Caymen, but in interactions with her friends, it's apparent that he doesn't really understand not everyone has a trust fund and multiple cars. It felt lacking.<br><br>It also made me uncomfortable that he was immediately interested in Caymen. Don't take this the wrong way, it was 100% instalove for me, but for a moment there, I did really feel as if she was his plebeian plaything of the moment. Their early meet-ups seemed a bit stalkery to me. I find it odd when a boy who doesn't go to the same school as you - and probably doesn't even live in the neighbourhood - goes out of his way to bring you your pre-sipped coco every morning, even though their small tradition was quite cute. What I will say in Xander's defence is that he was fully realised as a character. He was not merely a love interest, but a real, albeit spoiled, person in his own right.<br><br>As I already mentioned, the class divide is also where Susan comes in. (<i>I just remembered: Susan Meyers? That's a Desperate Housewives name right there! Oh, Kasie West, you sly minx.</i>) I honestly have to question this: which young, single mother (<i>my calculations say she was around eighteen when she got pregnant</i>) starts a doll shop when she has to provide for a young child? It doesn't seem all that practical and self-sufficient to me. I know there are collectors out there, who will pay a lot of money for eccentric trinkets, but it doesn't seem plausible to me that they survived on this income.<br><br>On the other hand, I appreciated the details West included in her portrayal of a poor family. In the beginning, Caymen and her mother are eating and there is no mention of meat. I liked this touch. For one, meat is expensive and secondly, the fact that Caymen doesn't even go "No meat, because we are poor." <i>shows</i> me that she's used to this situation but not bitter about it. I thought it was wonderful that West didn't make her protagonist a spoiled brat who just hates on being poor. Caymen has stamina and she works for what she wants. <br><br>On a side note, I'm also very glad that she has a strong interest in science. While science never really gripped me the way literature did, it's good that not all these YA heroines are poetry addicts or aspiring artists. Variety. Let's keep it that way. LOVE YOU, CAYMEN.<br><br>So, the ending was not good for me. The reveal about her grandparents was a cop-out and I never felt that the class issues were adequately addressed. The beginning was promising on that front and the first half of the book almost made me cry because Caymen really struggles with the class divide. Feels, feels, feels. I love you, Caymen! I was expecting heartbreaking events with a touch of drama and some angst sprinkled on top, but that particular storyline never delivered, in my opinion.<br><br> I feel horrible for hating on a HEA, because Caymen gets all the fuzzy endings she wants from me. Just personally, I would have loved some more ambiguity. Give her a couple good things, but not the whole shebang. That doesn't come across as authentic to me. Then again, I hail from the land of pessimists (<i>we like to think of ourselves as realists, but honestly, who are we kidding exactly?</i>), so that might just be me. LOVE YOU, CAYMEN.<br><br>Overall, I think <i>The Distance Between Us</i> is a very solid read. I will definitely reread it and see if I can make myself be more at peace with the way things turned out (<i>I doubt it though</i>). It has made me curious to explore more of the genre, so if anyone has any recs, they are welcome here! Most of all, it has made me extremely excited for West's <i>Pivot Point</i> series and just for her as a novelist in general. Good stuff. LOVE YOU, CAYMEN.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14905025504308170077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13579734750204892110"><b>*4.25 STARS!*</b><br/><br/>Ahhh, this is <u>SO CUTE</u>!<br/>I already read <i>The Fill-In Boyfriend</i> before and I thought that that was going to be my favorite Kasie West book, but boy was I wrong because I clearly hadn't read this one yet!<br/>I'm such a sucker for cute romance novels these days! The type where you don't have to think too hard, just the sit-back-and-enjoy-the-ride kind of stories. This one is a perfect example! It might be a bit predictable but it's just so adorable mixed with just the right amount of humor, I </span>
  <span id="freeText13579734750204892110" style="display:none"><b>*4.25 STARS!*</b><br /><br />Ahhh, this is <u>SO CUTE</u>!<br />I already read <i>The Fill-In Boyfriend</i> before and I thought that that was going to be my favorite Kasie West book, but boy was I wrong because I clearly hadn't read this one yet!<br />I'm such a sucker for cute romance novels these days! The type where you don't have to think too hard, just the sit-back-and-enjoy-the-ride kind of stories. This one is a perfect example! It might be a bit predictable but it's just so adorable mixed with just the right amount of humor, I couldn't help but love it.<br />This book deals with a lot of issues like poverty, health struggles, what to do with your future, family drama.. But not in an extremely heavy way and that's also part of what I liked so much about it.<br />What I didn't like about this is actually the same as what I liked about it, if that even makes sense. I feel like nothing really happened the whole time, except for <i>"girl meets boy", "girl falls in love with boy"</i> and <i>"girl figures things out"</i>. I would've liked this even more if there was a bit more excitement and more interesting stuff happening. Also, the ending felt a bit rushed and came really sudden, there were a lot of things still left in the dark, I still had so many questions! I like to read books like this in between heavier reads or long series though so I'm still giving it 4.25 stars. It made me happy and relaxed and that's exactly what I wanted :)<br />Overall, this was a really cute and very quick read. I'll definitely read more Kasie West in the future! <br /></span>

<div id="review_1684993186" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684993186?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062235664" href="/book/show/17251018-the-distance-between-us">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684993186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14877683849858745850">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maymay</a>, who also recommended this!<br/><br/><b>3.5</b><br/><br/>This buddy read was pretty much a spontaneous one. I was having a crisis over my slump which has been going on for a week and a half now and then May recommended I try out this one and she reread it with me! Having read PS I Like You earlier this year, I had high hopes a Kasie West book would fix my slump. I think it did! <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“His eyes are so intense I want to look away . . . or never look away, I can’t decide.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>The Distance Between Us is not a</span>
  <span id="freeText14877683849858745850" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">Maymay</a>, who also recommended this!<br /><br /><b>3.5</b><br /><br />This buddy read was pretty much a spontaneous one. I was having a crisis over my slump which has been going on for a week and a half now and then May recommended I try out this one and she reread it with me! Having read PS I Like You earlier this year, I had high hopes a Kasie West book would fix my slump. I think it did! <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“His eyes are so intense I want to look away . . . or never look away, I can’t decide.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The Distance Between Us is not as good as PS I Like You, but it's just as <b>adorable, light, and fluffy.</b> It was also super funny since our MC, Caymen is a pro when it comes to sarcasm and I just loved it. I connected with her on a spiritual level. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“So Caymen..."<br />"So, Xander..."<br />"Like the islands."<br />"What?"<br />"Your name. Caymen. Like the Cayman Islands. Is that your mom's favourite place to visit or something?"<br />"No, it's her third favourite place. I have an older brother named Paris and an older sister named Sydney."<br />"Wow." He opens the bag, takes out a muffin, and hands it to me. The top glistens with sprinkled sugar. "Really?"<br />I gently unwrap it. "No.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>BUT REAL TALK NOW. CAN WE GIVE ALL THE STARS TO XANDER?</b> He's the most precious thing in the entire world. He's so adorable and sweet and please, I need my own Xander, okay thank you and goodbye. <br /><br />I love Kasie's writing. So light and easy to fly through. And really addictive.<br /><br />Of course there were problems with this book, hence why it's not a 4 star like PS I Like You. Basically, it didn't have the exact magic PS I Like You had. Also, the ending was so incredibly rushed. The book had slow development and slow development which I really appreciated (but also wanted to scream at the book because PLEASE XANDER AND CAYMEN ARE SO ADORABLE AND I WANTED THEM TO GET TOGETHER QUICKLY???? Do you get my conflict??), but then towards the end, everything was super rushed. Caymen and Xander's relationship, Caymen's family problems, Caymen's own issues... everything was miraculously fixed in a few pages and I think I wouldn't have minded at all if the book was a bit longer. It was all a bit <i>too</i> unrealistic. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I turn my head so that he doesn't see my smile and secretly curse him for making me feel special.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>Read this book for Xander, guys.</b> For Xander and sarcasm and cuteness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14877683849858745850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer603065313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1626965610540023554">My good bud Flannery told me about this book. About how funny and cute and cool it was. It's a contemporary YA so it practically preordered itself for me.<br/><br/>I started it the day my postie left it in my mail box. I finished it that same night, well, 4am in the morning (reading into the squeaky hours of the night is one of my absolute favourite activities, but only the best* books can take me there).<br/><br/>The Distance Between Us is so much what I love about YA. It's smiley and fun and funny and has this ri</span>
  <span id="freeText1626965610540023554" style="display:none">My good bud Flannery told me about this book. About how funny and cute and cool it was. It's a contemporary YA so it practically preordered itself for me.<br /><br />I started it the day my postie left it in my mail box. I finished it that same night, well, 4am in the morning (reading into the squeaky hours of the night is one of my absolute favourite activities, but only the best* books can take me there).<br /><br />The Distance Between Us is so much what I love about YA. It's smiley and fun and funny and has this ridiculously swoony slow burn romance. Seriously. It also just felt unique. Like it was just marching along happily to it's own little beat.<br /><br />It has the best cool inclusions. I do not want to give everything away, but: living on top of a (creepy) doll shop! Grave-digging and cemeteries! Serenading musicians! Midnight pranks! op shopping! (or, as Americans would say: thrift stores!) Cute hot chocolate moments and a surprise plane flight. Oh! And that first kiss scene? Perfection &lt;3<br /><br />What makes a book unputdownable for me? Loving it. I just got right in the groove. I didn't want it to end. The swoon and zingy-fun-antagonistic-cute chemistry between Caymen and Xander = addictive.<br /><br />I loved the characters. Also, I mostly try not to think about the author while reading (my goals is to get lost in the land of make-believe) but I couldn't help but imagine just how much fun Kasie West must have had writing this book. So many grins -- awesome one-liners, cute scenes. Lots of swoon. And the plot itself was fun with creative settings.<br /><br />The ending has a twist that's a bit wild. I'm not sure it entirely works? But I could definitely work with it :) It did not detract from my enjoyment at all.<br /><br />I loved this. I had such a great time reading it. You all know I love contemporary YA and am always hunting for my next perfect fix. This book delivered. One of my favourite reads this year and a new lifetime contemporary favourite &lt;3 <br /><br />*best = my kind of books &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="1626965610540023554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_910907433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/910907433" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/910907433?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer910907433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9132837275443410567"><a href='http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/omg_zpsrv9ygqtg.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431350805ra/14828023.gif' alt=' photo omg_zpsrv9ygqtg.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Oh my dear, dear Kasie West...<b>Where have you been all my life??</b> Well, in all fairness, it's my fault I've never picked up a masterpiece that is a KW novel. My friend, Anna, has been more than clear about how I would love this author, if only for her adorable, yes, <b>absolutely adorable</b> male leads. And, ya know, she was right-as usual. Damn know it all Alien. Anyway, I digress. My whole point is that when I was down and tired and couldn't hardly read this weekend, what did I do? I listened to s</span>
  <span id="freeText9132837275443410567" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/omg_zpsrv9ygqtg.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431350805ra/14828023.gif" alt=" photo omg_zpsrv9ygqtg.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oh my dear, dear Kasie West...<b>Where have you been all my life??</b> Well, in all fairness, it's my fault I've never picked up a masterpiece that is a KW novel. My friend, Anna, has been more than clear about how I would love this author, if only for her adorable, yes, <b>absolutely adorable</b> male leads. And, ya know, she was right-as usual. Damn know it all Alien. Anyway, I digress. My whole point is that when I was down and tired and couldn't hardly read this weekend, what did I do? I listened to someone's advice and picked up a fun book that was supposed to be light, funny, and altogether an easy read. I've never been so glad I did. <br><br><br><b>He laughs a little. "You live above a porcelain-doll store; your best friend lives in a cemetery. You've pretty much grown up surrounded by creepy things. Is there anything you're afraid of?"<br>You.</b><br><br><br>I have been in a perpetual bad mood for the last two weeks-I won't lie about that. It's been horrible. I haven't cared about much and yes, I come off as (generally) pretty normal/happy most of the time. I've even found some amazing books to read. But, what happens when an already bad mood turns just plain sour the minute Thursday strikes? Why, you pick up a fluffy book. All the booze and/or medicine in the world couldn't salvage my mood, but guess what did? This book cured a two week streak of surliness and altogether inexcusable snark on my part. This book did what no person could do, no matter how hard they tried, and that's how I know I waited until the perfect time to start obsessing over this woman's books.<br><br><br><b>A lot of people don't get my humor. My mom calls it dry humor. I think that means "not funny," but it also means I'm the only one who ever knows it's a joke. Maybe if I laugh afterward, like my mom does when she's helping customers, more people would humor me, but I can't bring myself to do it.</b><br><br><br>It's more than that, though. I don't do cheesy. I loathe easy peasy story-lines, unless it's my dear Lauren Layne. And I don't really venture from my dystopian or fantasies very often-but for this author? I think I'm going to start making an exception. <b>From page one I was giggling, smiling ear-to-ear, and felt immediately lighter</b>. The snarkiness of our main character was parallel to some of my all time favorite snark-masters and Xander was...oh my, what was Xander? Xander was the equivalent to every good person in the world I feel like I would date. <br><br><br><b>After he climbs in as well, he starts the engine and then gives me a long look. "What's wrong, babe?" Xander grabs my hand and puts it on his knee.<br>"Is that the pet name we're going with? Babe?"<br>He backs out of the parking stall and starts driving. "You don't like it?"<br>"It's okay. It makes me think of the pig, though."<br>"Are you putting in a request, then?"<br>"I've always been partial to sweetie, mostly because I'm not sweet so it makes me laugh."</b><br><br><br>I don't know. He just...there was just something so special about him. He may have been rich and a tad spoiled, but it never once showed in his demeanor and he never let it effect who he was as a person (namely, he didn't act like a pompous, spoiled brat). Sure, he might have worn driving gloves (BAHAHA okay, that was unnecessary of me to say, but come on, Xander-driving gloves?? LMAO) and he may not own anything shoddier than a high-brow polo, expensive jeans, and loafers, but he was a total boy-next-door type, and his sweetness never once effected me as it does with other books. <b>I like dark, tortured guys the most, lately</b>, but I also have <i>always</i> had a soft spot for the good ones. Those boys that we should all aspire to date, if they existed beyond these pages. And yeah, my heart is super easy to break into (and break, when it comes to book boys) but lately the boys in these stories have had to work really hard for my fangirl affection....But with Xander? <b>It was effortless.</b><br><br><br><b>He pockets his phone. "Caymen."<br>"Xander."<br>"Does this mean I won the game?"<br>"I didn't realize we were playing a game."<br>He picks up the doll and backs away with his lower-lip-biting smile. "I think you did."</b><br><br><br>Even now as I am finishing up this review my heart is soaring and I have the biggest smile on my face as I recall my favorite quotes and moments from this story. It wasn't without it's flaws, much like any other book, but the flaws were hardly a blip on my radar. But, hey, that's the way I am. <b>I truly believe that, if a book made you extremely happy and you weren't without warm and blissful feelings throughout, it deserves every star in the world.</b> But that's only if the flaws don't outweigh the good-in that case, yeah, it probably stunted your enjoyment a tad. But, even with some of the miscommunications and rude preconceived notions, my smile never slipped once (Okay, lie, there was definitely some angst that made me frowny face-but only because I love my dear Xander so much!!!). <br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/3118900_zpspug483gh.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430508671ra/14721474.gif" alt=" photo 3118900_zpspug483gh.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>So, you know, I loved this. The rich, <i>beckoning</i> boy and the not-so-rich girl meeting and finding a spark they've never felt before, mixed with funny shenanigans to find each other's destiny, <b>this story was perfection</b>. From the way Xander looked at Caymen all the way to how much he was willing to do to make her a part of his life-I couldn't put this one down. <b>Pre-sipped drinks and bakery made blueberry muffins never sounded so wonderful</b>, thanks to Xander, and I know I'll be re-reading this many times over if only to read about Xander's hard earned smiles and Caymen curiosities. Anna, I owe you one, ya ol' dark pup. :P <br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u></span>
  <a data-text-id="9132837275443410567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661072108" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661072108?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661072108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9183381887619693626"><u>The Girl.</u> HAS Sarcasm down to an art. As is, said fact was enough to have me more than like the girl. There’s more though like her being loyal and an all around good girl though not too goody-goody to have her seeming stick in the mud. <br/><br/><u>The Guy.</u> IS the definition of cool. And smooth. What with the perceived beckoning and all, yes? (Have I mentioned smooth?)<br/><br/><u>Between them.</u> IS gap made wider then wider still by a number of things like (a) mothers and their secrets, (b) these kids and their assumption</span>
  <span id="freeText9183381887619693626" style="display:none"><u>The Girl.</u> HAS Sarcasm down to an art. As is, said fact was enough to have me more than like the girl. There’s more though like her being loyal and an all around good girl though not too goody-goody to have her seeming stick in the mud. <br /><br /><u>The Guy.</u> IS the definition of cool. And smooth. What with the perceived beckoning and all, yes? (Have I mentioned smooth?)<br /><br /><u>Between them.</u> IS gap made wider then wider still by a number of things like (a) mothers and their secrets, (b) these kids and their assumptions PLUS a whole lot of one or the other jumping the gun because of the same! (c) Some of the interesting ‘others’ complicate matters further though those really ought not be so complicated. <br /><br />It’s all these complications that have me thinking adorbs (see if you can count how many times I use this word in reference to Caymen, Caymen and Alex or anyone in this book for that matter.) But by golly! This book is the definition of CUTE: <br /><br />-See me grin as I recall his moment at the end. <br />-See me grin as I recall how perfect each exchange between them went. Each moment made better because the guy ‘got’ her and she, him. Theirs is a sweet connection that had me excited at the possibilities of ‘them;’ then frustrated at all those things that got in the way of the same. <br /><br />-And yet again, witness how I’m still grinning over how their not so different set up has yielded such an utterly likeable pair. It’s not original: this rich boy/poorer girl divide, but the two of them take that trope and make something else out of it… and make me love them more for doing so! Her with her wit and him all suave, are not too obsessed over that bit. <br /><br />But things got even cuter with each thing they’d do for the other. It’s obvious that theirs is more than instant attraction (though there’s that too) because there’s a building of something more between them with the both of them seeing the other in some way the object didn’t even consider. They bring out the new in each other and were adorable while at it! <br /><br />(Seriously, make me stop grinning.) <br /><br />****<br /><i>Readers of all things cute and contemporary, this book's for you</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9183381887619693626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4410112655191534770">This is my <b>3rd</b> book of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West' title='Kasie West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kasie West</a>,and I think she is now,one of my favorite authors,because I do enjoy her writing style and I want to thank my buddy,<b>NEIL</b> for introducing this author to me!^^<br/><br/>This book is such an easy,very relaxing read! The story though is a bit predictable,but it was interesting because I enjoyed the main characters (<b>Caymen and Xander</b>) development. I loved the witty,sarcastic humor of Caymen,and the way she interacts with people cracks me up all the time.Xander,the charming ric</span>
  <span id="freeText4410112655191534770" style="display:none">This is my <b>3rd</b> book of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a>,and I think she is now,one of my favorite authors,because I do enjoy her writing style and I want to thank my buddy,<b>NEIL</b> for introducing this author to me!^^<br><br>This book is such an easy,very relaxing read! The story though is a bit predictable,but it was interesting because I enjoyed the main characters (<b>Caymen and Xander</b>) development. I loved the witty,sarcastic humor of Caymen,and the way she interacts with people cracks me up all the time.Xander,the charming rich boy or the live version of Ken(Barbie doll's sweetheart) is incredibly swoon-worthy,sweet and thoughtful,and I loved the growth of their cute,romantic relationship which started from total strangers to friends,to <b>"career day dates"</b>(Ooh,I totally adored those part,lol!)<br><br>I thoroughly enjoyed reading this book,but there had been a little twist in the story that I found a bit weird..but still,I liked the ending.<br><br>I want to thank my sweet friend,<b>Boots</b> for recommending this book to me. <br><b>Hope you'll also check her captivating review on this,as your way of honoring her birthday today.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453925944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9745100834723130812"><b>*please ignore sentences that don't make sense and spelling errors I was high on xander when I wrote this and have already edited twice don't have more energy</b><br/><br/>Before I begin, I’d like to have a moment of silence for Xander’s smile (the one I’m never waking up to in this lifetime) because from what I’ve heard, it’s pretty darn good.<br/><b><br/>I mean, there’s this:</b><br/><br/><i>He throws me his smile. I swear the thing could end wars.</i><br/><b><br/>and this:</b><br/><br/><i>He smiles. I love his smile. I don’t want to talk about my mom. I want to talk ab</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9745100834723130812" style="display:none"><b>*please ignore sentences that don't make sense and spelling errors I was high on xander when I wrote this and have already edited twice don't have more energy</b><br><br>Before I begin, I’d like to have a moment of silence for Xander’s smile (the one I’m never waking up to in this lifetime) because from what I’ve heard, it’s pretty darn good.<br><b><br>I mean, there’s this:</b><br><br><i>He throws me his smile. I swear the thing could end wars.</i><br><b><br>and this:</b><br><br><i>He smiles. I love his smile. I don’t want to talk about my mom. I want to talk about his smile or kissing. I could talk about kissing.</i><br><br><b>and this:</b><br><br><i>He offers me his lower-lip-biting smile and I almost rush into his arms. For the first time since I walked away from him the other night my heart feels whole.</i><br><br><b>I NEED MY XANDER. IF ANYONE CAN TELL ME WHERE TO SIGN UP FOR ONE, I'D BE ETERNALLY GRATEFUL.</b><br><br>The thing about contemporaries is, there’s hardly any variation. And despite how cute this one was, it went more or less the way I could’ve guessed it went. It even involved the <i>you’re-not-like-other-girls</i> trope, but I’m not going to judge <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a> for it, because <b>dammit I love Caymen and Xander so much I need them to be real so I can third wheel all the time.</b><br><br><b>PROS:</b> XANDER SPENCE. <b>CONS:</b> Extreme cheesiness (side effects: nausea and sprained muscles due to smiling to much)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486728555i/21944234._SY540_.png" width="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

CUTE.<br/><br/>The first time I read this I gave it 5 stars instantly but now that I’m rereading it, I’ve noticed A LOT more flaws than my fetus self who had no standards. <br/><br/>Dropping this to a 3 is painful for me but if somehow by a GREAT miracle half stars were to appear, I would give it a confident 3.5 stars but alas I cannot so here we are.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492184022i/22491358._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If we’re judging by cuteness, this wins that award for the next ten years.<br/>Hot chocolate<br/>Muffins <br/>Cay</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie Shores" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Shores" href="/user/show/25177308-bonnie-shores">Bonnie Shores</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=teen-life">teen-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2341710581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10583498397818127515">Basically, I'm a sucker for cheesy romances, especially ones where the guy is unrealistically perfect—handsome, wealthy, smart, sweet and sincere, i.e., Xander Spence.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523031238ra/25335298.gif' width='600' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When Xander walks into Caymen's mom's doll store (nicknamed Little Shop of Horrors by her free-spirited best friend), she knows right away that he's not for her. He oozes rich, while Caymen and her mom live above the doll store in a tiny apartment and barely make ends meet. He unwittingly makes a bad first impression and is summari</span>
  <span id="freeText10583498397818127515" style="display:none">Basically, I'm a sucker for cheesy romances, especially ones where the guy is unrealistically perfect—handsome, wealthy, smart, sweet and sincere, i.e., Xander Spence.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523031238ra/25335298.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Xander walks into Caymen's mom's doll store (nicknamed Little Shop of Horrors by her free-spirited best friend), she knows right away that he's not for her. He oozes rich, while Caymen and her mom live above the doll store in a tiny apartment and barely make ends meet. He unwittingly makes a bad first impression and is summarily dismissed by Caymen's natural sarcasm.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523032765ra/25335426.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That doesn't stop Xander from trying to get to know Caymen, though. He enjoys her sarcasm and dry wit, finding her different from his normal circle of friends. He does lots of little things that have big meaning and Caymen begins to fall for him, despite her best intentions.<br><br>This is <i>kind of</i> a modern take on the old Cinderella story, a great choice when you want a quick, cute, clean romance that leaves you smiling.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1523032531ra/25335383.gif" width="600" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x8G8/Aha9DWxbQ56Fva2tU61eyxGXxuRWSaoj6msIv8mxpXPMOLu8k0pguQTnVqK6kVBG4DMyRaT+67+AqwOoA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mbLxCJqPrwrZ50TSt9xEOZN84P0cC1LKyNnshFdSfgl4tdg7oje1zSWjyEyyt6gGN4zaytqYgE0CBOr1/FJSVg==')})
  }
